<td colspan="2" style="text-align:center;text-align:left; font-size:smaller">Rankings include all <a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">provinces and territories</a></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><b>Nova Scotia</b> (<span class="nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'n' in 'nigh'">n</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="'v' in 'vie'">v</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span> <span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="'k' in 'kind'">k</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="/ʃ/: 'sh' in 'shy'">ʃ</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Latin_language" title="Latin language">Latin</a> for "New Scotland"; <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <span lang="fr"><i>Nouvelle-Écosse</i></span>; <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic_language" title="Scottish Gaelic language">Scottish Gaelic</a>: <span lang="gd"><i>Alba Nuadh</i></span>) is one of <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">Canada</a>'s three <a href="/wiki/The_Maritimes" title="The Maritimes">Maritime</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canadian_Province" title="Canadian Province">provinces</a>, and one of the four provinces which form <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Canada" title="Atlantic Canada">Atlantic Canada</a>. Its provincial capital is <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_Nova_Scotia" title="Halifax, Nova Scotia">Halifax</a>. Nova Scotia is the second smallest of Canada's ten provinces, with an area of 55,284 square kilometres (21,300 sq mi), including <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Island" title="Cape Breton Island">Cape Breton</a> and another 3,800 coastal islands. As of 2016, the population was 923,598. Nova Scotia is the second most-densely populated province in Canada with 17.4 inhabitants per square kilometre (45/sq mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2016census_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-2016census-1">[1]</a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Etymology">Etymology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Etymology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>"Nova Scotia" means "New Scotland" in Latin<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup> and is the recognized <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English language</a> name for the province. In <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Gaelic" title="Scottish Gaelic">Scottish Gaelic</a>, the province is called <i><span lang="gd">Alba Nuadh</span></i>, which also simply means "New Scotland". The province was first named in the 1621 Royal Charter granting the right to settle lands including modern Nova Scotia, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Island" title="Cape Breton Island">Cape Breton Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Island" title="Prince Edward Island">Prince Edward Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Gasp%C3%A9_Peninsula" title="Gaspé Peninsula">Gaspé Peninsula</a> to <a href="/wiki/William_Alexander,_1st_Earl_of_Stirling" title="William Alexander, 1st Earl of Stirling">Sir William Alexander</a> in 1632.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-royalcharter_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-royalcharter-6">[6]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Annapolis_Valley,_Nova_Scotia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4912" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Annapolis_Valley%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg/220px-Annapolis_Valley%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Annapolis_Valley%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg/330px-Annapolis_Valley%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/Annapolis_Valley%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg/440px-Annapolis_Valley%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Geography of Nova Scotia">Geography of Nova Scotia</a></div>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_provincial_parks_in_Nova_Scotia" title="List of provincial parks in Nova Scotia">List of provincial parks in Nova Scotia</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_protected_areas_of_Nova_Scotia" title="List of protected areas of Nova Scotia">List of protected areas of Nova Scotia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:NS_koppen.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="945" data-file-width="900" height="231" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/NS_koppen.svg/220px-NS_koppen.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/NS_koppen.svg/330px-NS_koppen.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/NS_koppen.svg/440px-NS_koppen.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nova_Scotia-map-2.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="608" data-file-width="652" height="280" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Nova_Scotia-map-2.png/300px-Nova_Scotia-map-2.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Nova_Scotia-map-2.png/450px-Nova_Scotia-map-2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/07/Nova_Scotia-map-2.png/600px-Nova_Scotia-map-2.png 2x" width="300"/></a>

</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Novascotia_topo.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1596" data-file-width="2000" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Novascotia_topo.png/300px-Novascotia_topo.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Novascotia_topo.png/450px-Novascotia_topo.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Novascotia_topo.png/600px-Novascotia_topo.png 2x" width="300"/></a>

<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Novascotia_topo.png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Topography of Nova Scotia.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Nova Scotia is Canada's smallest province in area after <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Island" title="Prince Edward Island">Prince Edward Island</a>. The province's mainland is the <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_peninsula" title="Nova Scotia peninsula">Nova Scotia peninsula</a> surrounded by the Atlantic Ocean, including numerous bays and estuaries. Nowhere in Nova Scotia is more than 67 km (42 mi) from the ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Island" title="Cape Breton Island">Cape Breton Island</a>, a large island to the northeast of the Nova Scotia mainland, is also part of the province, as is <a href="/wiki/Sable_Island" title="Sable Island">Sable Island</a>, a small island notorious for its shipwrecks,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> approximately 175 km (110 mi) from the province's southern coast.</p>
<p>Nova Scotia has many ancient fossil-bearing rock formations. These formations are particularly rich on the Bay of Fundy's shores. Blue Beach near <a href="/wiki/Hantsport" title="Hantsport">Hantsport</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Joggins_Fossil_Cliffs" title="Joggins Fossil Cliffs">Joggins Fossil Cliffs</a>, on the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Fundy" title="Bay of Fundy">Bay of Fundy</a>'s shores, has yielded an abundance of <a href="/wiki/Carboniferous" title="Carboniferous">Carboniferous</a> age fossils. Wasson's Bluff, near the town of <a href="/wiki/Parrsboro" title="Parrsboro">Parrsboro</a>, has yielded both <a href="/wiki/Triassic" title="Triassic">Triassic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jurassic" title="Jurassic">Jurassic</a> age fossils.</p>
<p>The province contains 5,400 lakes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Climate of Nova Scotia">Climate of Nova Scotia</a></div>
<p>Nova Scotia lies in the mid-temperate zone. Since the province is almost surrounded by the sea, the climate is closer to <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_climate" title="Oceanic climate">maritime</a> than to <a href="/wiki/Continental_climate" title="Continental climate">continental climate</a>. The winter and summer temperature extremes of the continental climate are moderated by the ocean.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ECclimate_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-ECclimate-10">[10]</a></sup> However, winters are still cold enough to be classified as continental – still being nearer the freezing point than inland areas to the west. The Nova Scotia climate is in many ways similar to the central <a href="/wiki/Baltic_Sea" title="Baltic Sea">Baltic Sea</a> coast in Northern Europe, only wetter and snowier. This is in spite of Nova Scotia being some fifteen parallels south. Areas not on the Atlantic coast experience warmer summers more typical of inland areas, and winter lows a little colder.</p>
<p>Described on the provincial vehicle-licence plate as Canada's Ocean Playground, Nova Scotia is surrounded by four major bodies of water: the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Saint_Lawrence" title="Gulf of Saint Lawrence">Gulf of Saint Lawrence</a> to the north, the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Fundy" title="Bay of Fundy">Bay of Fundy</a> to the west, the <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Maine" title="Gulf of Maine">Gulf of Maine</a> to the southwest, and Atlantic Ocean to the east.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ECclimate_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-ECclimate-10">[10]</a></sup></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Nova_Scotia" title="History of Nova Scotia">History of Nova Scotia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Military_history_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Military history of Nova Scotia">Military history of Nova Scotia</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Overview">Overview</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Overview">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The province includes regions of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mi%27kmaq_people" title="Mi'kmaq people">Mi'kmaq</a> nation of Mi'kma'ki (<i><span lang="mic">mi'gama'gi</span></i>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> The Mi'kmaq people inhabited Nova Scotia at the time the first European colonists arrived.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> In 1605, <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">French</a> colonists established the first permanent European settlement in the future Canada (and the first north of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Florida" title="Spanish Florida">Florida</a>) at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habitation_at_Port-Royal" title="Habitation at Port-Royal">Port Royal</a>, founding what would become known as <a href="/wiki/Acadia" title="Acadia">Acadia</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morton1999_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morton1999-14">[14]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup></p>
<p>The British <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Port_Royal_(1710)" title="Siege of Port Royal (1710)">conquest of Acadia</a> took place in 1710. The <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Utrecht" title="Treaty of Utrecht">Treaty of Utrecht</a> in 1713 formally recognized this and returned <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Island" title="Cape Breton Island">Cape Breton Island</a> (<i><span lang="fr">Île Royale</span></i>) to the French. Present-day New Brunswick then still formed a part of the French colony of Acadia. The British changed<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (June 2016)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> the name of the capital from Port Royal to <a href="/wiki/Annapolis_Royal" title="Annapolis Royal">Annapolis Royal</a>. In 1749, the capital of Nova Scotia moved from <a href="/wiki/Annapolis_Royal" title="Annapolis Royal">Annapolis Royal</a> to the newly established <a href="/wiki/Halifax,_Nova_Scotia" title="Halifax, Nova Scotia">Halifax</a>. In 1755 the vast majority of the French population (the Acadians) were forcibly removed in the <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Acadians" title="Expulsion of the Acadians">Expulsion of the Acadians</a>; <a href="/wiki/New_England_Planters" title="New England Planters">New England Planters</a> arrived between 1759 and 1768 to replace them.</p>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:752px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Port_Royal_today.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1856" data-file-width="8192" height="170" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Port_Royal_today.jpg/750px-Port_Royal_today.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Port_Royal_today.jpg/1125px-Port_Royal_today.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7d/Port_Royal_today.jpg/1500px-Port_Royal_today.jpg 2x" width="750"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Port_Royal_today.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Port_Royal,_Annapolis_County,_Nova_Scotia" title="Port Royal, Annapolis County, Nova Scotia">Port Royal, Annapolis County, Nova Scotia</a>, situated on the Annapolis River where it widens to form the Annapolis Basin</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1763, most of Acadia (Cape Breton Island, St. John's Island (now <a href="/wiki/Prince_Edward_Island" title="Prince Edward Island">Prince Edward Island</a>), and New Brunswick) became part of Nova Scotia. In 1769, St. John's Island became a separate colony. Nova Scotia included present-day <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a> until that province's establishment in 1784, after the arrival of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_Empire_Loyalists" title="United Empire Loyalists">United Empire Loyalists</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> In 1867, Nova Scotia became one of the four founding provinces of the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Confederation" title="Canadian Confederation">Canadian Confederation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ReferenceA_17-0"><a href="#cite_note-ReferenceA-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="17th_and_18th_centuries">17th and 18th centuries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 17th and 18th centuries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:FortEdwardWindsorNovaScotiaCanada.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1536" data-file-width="2048" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/FortEdwardWindsorNovaScotiaCanada.JPG/170px-FortEdwardWindsorNovaScotiaCanada.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/FortEdwardWindsorNovaScotiaCanada.JPG/255px-FortEdwardWindsorNovaScotiaCanada.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/FortEdwardWindsorNovaScotiaCanada.JPG/340px-FortEdwardWindsorNovaScotiaCanada.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:FortEdwardWindsorNovaScotiaCanada.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Fort_Edward_(Nova_Scotia)" title="Fort Edward (Nova Scotia)">Fort Edward</a> – the oldest <a href="/wiki/Blockhouse" title="Blockhouse">blockhouse</a> in North America (1750).</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:A_View_of_Louisburg_in_North_America_(cropped).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="394" data-file-width="621" height="140" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/A_View_of_Louisburg_in_North_America_%28cropped%29.jpg/220px-A_View_of_Louisburg_in_North_America_%28cropped%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/A_View_of_Louisburg_in_North_America_%28cropped%29.jpg/330px-A_View_of_Louisburg_in_North_America_%28cropped%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/A_View_of_Louisburg_in_North_America_%28cropped%29.jpg/440px-A_View_of_Louisburg_in_North_America_%28cropped%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:A_View_of_Louisburg_in_North_America_(cropped).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A View of Louisburg in North America, November 11, 1762.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The warfare on Nova Scotian soil during the 17th and 18th centuries significantly influenced the history of Nova Scotia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability"><span title="Quotation needed from source to verify. (June 2016)">need quotation to verify</span></a></i>]</sup> The Mi'kmaq had lived in Nova Scotia for centuries. The French arrived in 1604, and Catholic Mi'kmaq and Acadians formed the majority of the population of the colony for the next 150 years. During the first 80 years the French and Acadians lived in Nova Scotia, nine significant military clashes took place as the English and Scottish (later British), <a href="/wiki/Jurriaen_Aernoutsz" title="Jurriaen Aernoutsz">Dutch</a> and French fought for possession of the area. These encounters happened at <a href="/wiki/Port_Royal,_Annapolis_County,_Nova_Scotia" title="Port Royal, Annapolis County, Nova Scotia">Port Royal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_John,_New_Brunswick" title="Saint John, New Brunswick">Saint John</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup> Cap de Sable (present-day <a href="/wiki/Port_La_Tour,_Nova_Scotia" title="Port La Tour, Nova Scotia">Port La Tour, Nova Scotia</a>), <a href="/wiki/Jemseg,_New_Brunswick" title="Jemseg, New Brunswick">Jemseg</a> (1674 and 1758) and <a href="/wiki/Baleine,_Nova_Scotia" title="Baleine, Nova Scotia">Baleine</a> (1629). The <a href="/wiki/Acadian_Civil_War" title="Acadian Civil War">Acadian Civil War</a> took place from 1640 to 1645.</p>
<p>Beginning with <a href="/wiki/King_William%27s_War" title="King William's War">King William's War</a> in 1688, six wars took place in Nova Scotia before the British defeated the French (and ultimately expelled much of their population) and made peace with the Mi'kmaq:</p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/King_William%27s_War" title="King William's War">King William's War</a> (1688–1697),</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Queen_Anne%27s_War" title="Queen Anne's War">Queen Anne's War</a> (1702–1713),</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Father_Rale%27s_War" title="Father Rale's War">Father Rale's War</a> (1722–1725),</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/King_George%27s_War" title="King George's War">King George's War</a> (1744–1748),</li>
<li><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Father_Le_Loutre%E2%80%99s_War" title="Father Le Loutre’s War">Father Le Loutre’s War</a> (1749–1755)</li>
<li>The Seven Years' War, also called the <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">French and Indian War</a> (1754–1763)</li>
</ul>
<p>The battles during these wars took place primarily <a href="/wiki/Port_Royal,_Annapolis_County,_Nova_Scotia" title="Port Royal, Annapolis County, Nova Scotia">Port Royal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_John,_New_Brunswick" title="Saint John, New Brunswick">Saint John</a>, <a href="/wiki/Canso,_Nova_Scotia" title="Canso, Nova Scotia">Canso</a>, <a href="/wiki/Isthmus_of_Chignecto" title="Isthmus of Chignecto">Chignecto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Raid_on_Dartmouth_(1751)" title="Raid on Dartmouth (1751)">Dartmouth</a> (1751), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Raid_on_Lunenburg_(1756)" title="Raid on Lunenburg (1756)">Lunenburg</a> (1756) and <a href="/wiki/Grand-Pr%C3%A9,_Nova_Scotia" title="Grand-Pré, Nova Scotia">Grand-Pré</a>. Despite the British <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Port_Royal_(1710)" title="Siege of Port Royal (1710)">conquest of Acadia</a> in 1710, Nova Scotia remained primarily occupied by Catholic Acadians and Mi'kmaq, who confined British forces to Annapolis and to Canso.</p>
<p>The Mi'kmaq signed a series of peace and friendship treaties with <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a>, beginning after <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Father_Rale%27s_War" title="Father Rale's War">Father Rale's War</a> (1725). In 1725, the British signed a treaty (or "agreement") with the Mi'kmaq, but the authorities<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (June 2016)">which?</span></a></i>]</sup> have often disputed its definition of the rights of the Mi'kmaq to hunt and fish on their lands.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Glooscap_monument,_Millbrook,_Nova_Scotia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4912" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Glooscap_monument%2C_Millbrook%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg/220px-Glooscap_monument%2C_Millbrook%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Glooscap_monument%2C_Millbrook%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg/330px-Glooscap_monument%2C_Millbrook%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Glooscap_monument%2C_Millbrook%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg/440px-Glooscap_monument%2C_Millbrook%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Glooscap_monument,_Millbrook,_Nova_Scotia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Monument at Millbrook, near Truro, Nova Scotia paying tribute to Glooscap--a legendary figure to Mi'kmaq people of Nova Scotia.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A generation later, <a href="/wiki/Father_Le_Loutre%27s_War" title="Father Le Loutre's War">Father Le Loutre's War</a> began when <a href="/wiki/Edward_Cornwallis" title="Edward Cornwallis">Edward Cornwallis</a> arrived to establish <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Halifax_Regional_Municipality" title="Halifax Regional Municipality">Halifax</a> with 13 transports on June 21, 1749.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> A General Court, made up of the governor and the Council, was the highest court in the colony at the time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nscourts_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-nscourts-24">[24]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Belcher_(jurist)" title="Jonathan Belcher (jurist)">Jonathan Belcher</a> was sworn in as chief justice of the Nova Scotia Supreme Court on October 21, 1754.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nscourts_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-nscourts-24">[24]</a></sup> The first legislative assembly in Halifax, under the Governorship of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Lawrence_(British_Army_officer)" title="Charles Lawrence (British Army officer)">Charles Lawrence</a>, met on October 2, 1758.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> During the <a href="/wiki/French_and_Indian_War" title="French and Indian War">French and Indian War</a> of 1754–63 (the North American theatre of the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years' War">Seven Years' War</a> of 1756-1763), the British <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Acadians" title="Expulsion of the Acadians">deported</a> the Acadians and recruited <a href="/wiki/New_England_Planters" title="New England Planters">New England Planters</a> to resettle the colony. The 75-year period of war ended with the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Burying_the_Hatchet_Ceremony_(Nova_Scotia)" title="Burying the Hatchet Ceremony (Nova Scotia)">Burial of the Hatchet Ceremony</a> between the British and the Mi'kmaq (1761). After the war, some Acadians were allowed to return and the British made treaties with the Mi’kmaq.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grand_Pre,_Nova_Scotia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2816" data-file-width="2112" height="227" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Grand_Pre%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg/170px-Grand_Pre%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Grand_Pre%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg/255px-Grand_Pre%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Grand_Pre%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg/340px-Grand_Pre%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Grand_Pre,_Nova_Scotia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
This church at Grand Pre, Nova Scotia, commemorates the beginning of the Acadian expulsion where the men were gathered to hear their fate from the British in 1755.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/American_Revolution" title="American Revolution">American Revolution</a> (1775–1783) had a significant impact on shaping Nova Scotia. Initially, Nova Scotia – "the 14th American Colony" as some called it – displayed ambivalence over whether the colony should join the more southern colonies in their defiance of Britain, and rebellion flared at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Cumberland" title="Battle of Fort Cumberland">Battle of Fort Cumberland</a> (1776) and at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siege_of_Saint_John_(1777)" title="Siege of Saint John (1777)">Siege of Saint John (1777)</a>. Throughout the war, American <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Privateers" title="Privateers">privateers</a> devastated the maritime economy by capturing ships and looting almost every community outside of Halifax. These American raids alienated many sympathetic or neutral Nova Scotians into supporting the British. By the end of the war Nova Scotia had outfitted a number of privateers to attack American shipping.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> British military forces based at Halifax succeeded in preventing American support for rebels in Nova Scotia and deterred any invasion of Nova Scotia. However the British navy failed to establish naval supremacy. While the British captured many American privateers in battles such as the <a href="/wiki/Naval_battle_off_Halifax" title="Naval battle off Halifax">Naval battle off Halifax</a> (1782), many more continued attacks on shipping and settlements until the final months of the war. The Royal Navy struggled to maintain British supply lines, defending convoys from American and French attacks as in the fiercely fought convoy battle, the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naval_battle_off_Cape_Breton" title="Naval battle off Cape Breton">Naval battle off Cape Breton</a> (1781).</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Birchtown,_Nova_Scotia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2736" data-file-width="3648" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Birchtown%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg/170px-Birchtown%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Birchtown%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg/255px-Birchtown%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/67/Birchtown%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg/340px-Birchtown%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Birchtown,_Nova_Scotia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
An interpretive sign along the Heritage Trail at the Black Loyalist Heritage Society's Birchtown museum.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>After the Thirteen Colonies and their French allies forced the British forces to surrender (1781), approximately 33,000 <a href="/wiki/Loyalist_(American_Revolution)" title="Loyalist (American Revolution)">Tories or Loyalists</a> (the King's Loyal Americans, allowed to place "<a href="/wiki/United_Empire_Loyalist" title="United Empire Loyalist">United Empire Loyalist</a>" after their names) settled in Nova Scotia (14,000 of them in what became New Brunswick) on lands granted by the Crown as some compensation for their losses. (The British administration divided Nova Scotia and carved out the present-day province of <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a> in 1784). The Loyalist exodus created new communities across Nova Scotia, including <a href="/wiki/Shelburne,_Nova_Scotia" title="Shelburne, Nova Scotia">Shelburne</a>, which briefly became one of the larger British settlements in North America, and infused Nova Scotia with additional capital and skills. However the migration also caused political tensions between Loyalist <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Leader" title="Leader">leaders</a> and the leaders of the existing <a href="/wiki/New_England_Planters" title="New England Planters">New England Planters</a> settlement. The Loyalist influx also pushed Nova Scotia's Mi'kmaq People to the margins as Loyalist land grants encroached on ill-defined native lands. As part of the Loyalist migration, about 3,000 <a href="/wiki/Black_Loyalist" title="Black Loyalist">Black Loyalists</a> arrived; they founded the largest free Black settlement in North America at <a href="/wiki/Birchtown,_Nova_Scotia" title="Birchtown, Nova Scotia">Birchtown</a>, near Shelburne. However unfair treatment and harsh conditions caused about one-third of the Black Loyalists to resettle in <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Leone" title="Sierra Leone">Sierra Leone</a> in 1792, where they founded <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Freetown,_Sierra_Leone" title="Freetown, Sierra Leone">Freetown</a> and became known in Africa as the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nova_Scotian_Settlers_(Sierra_Leone)" title="Nova Scotian Settlers (Sierra Leone)">Nova Scotian Settlers</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="19th_century">19th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 19th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:JoasephHoweStatue.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="692" data-file-width="921" height="128" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/JoasephHoweStatue.jpg/170px-JoasephHoweStatue.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/JoasephHoweStatue.jpg/255px-JoasephHoweStatue.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/JoasephHoweStatue.jpg/340px-JoasephHoweStatue.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:JoasephHoweStatue.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Statue of <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Howe" title="Joseph Howe">Joseph Howe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Province_House_(Nova_Scotia)" title="Province House (Nova Scotia)">Province House</a>, created by famed Quebec sculptor <a href="/wiki/Louis-Philippe_H%C3%A9bert" title="Louis-Philippe Hébert">Louis-Philippe Hébert</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/War_of_1812" title="War of 1812">War of 1812</a>, Nova Scotia's contribution to the British war effort involved communities either purchasing or building various privateer ships to attack U.S. vessels.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Perhaps the most dramatic moment in the war for Nova Scotia occurred when <a href="/wiki/HMS_Shannon_(1806)" title="HMS Shannon (1806)">HMS <i>Shannon</i></a> escorted the captured American frigate <a href="/wiki/USS_Chesapeake_(1799)" title="USS Chesapeake (1799)">USS <i>Chesapeake</i></a> into <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Harbour" title="Halifax Harbour">Halifax Harbour</a> (1813). Many of the U.S. prisoners were kept at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deadman%27s_Island,_Halifax" title="Deadman's Island, Halifax">Deadman's Island, Halifax</a>.</p>
<p>During this century, Nova Scotia became the first colony in <a href="/wiki/British_North_America" title="British North America">British North America</a> and in the <a href="/wiki/British_Empire" title="British Empire">British Empire</a> to achieve <a href="/wiki/Responsible_government" title="Responsible government">responsible government</a> in January–February 1848 and become <a href="/wiki/Self-governing_colony" title="Self-governing colony">self-governing</a> through the efforts of <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Howe" title="Joseph Howe">Joseph Howe</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> Nova Scotia had established <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Representative_government" title="Representative government">representative government</a> in 1758, an achievement later commemorated by the erection of the <a href="/wiki/Sir_Sandford_Fleming_Park" title="Sir Sandford Fleming Park">Dingle Tower</a> in 1908.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Welsford-Parker_Monument_at_the_entrance_to_the_Old_Burying_Ground_in_Halifax,_Nova_Scotia,_Canada.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1022" data-file-width="1280" height="136" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Welsford-Parker_Monument_at_the_entrance_to_the_Old_Burying_Ground_in_Halifax%2C_Nova_Scotia%2C_Canada.jpg/170px-Welsford-Parker_Monument_at_the_entrance_to_the_Old_Burying_Ground_in_Halifax%2C_Nova_Scotia%2C_Canada.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Welsford-Parker_Monument_at_the_entrance_to_the_Old_Burying_Ground_in_Halifax%2C_Nova_Scotia%2C_Canada.jpg/255px-Welsford-Parker_Monument_at_the_entrance_to_the_Old_Burying_Ground_in_Halifax%2C_Nova_Scotia%2C_Canada.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/91/Welsford-Parker_Monument_at_the_entrance_to_the_Old_Burying_Ground_in_Halifax%2C_Nova_Scotia%2C_Canada.jpg/340px-Welsford-Parker_Monument_at_the_entrance_to_the_Old_Burying_Ground_in_Halifax%2C_Nova_Scotia%2C_Canada.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Welsford-Parker_Monument_at_the_entrance_to_the_Old_Burying_Ground_in_Halifax,_Nova_Scotia,_Canada.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Welsford-Parker_Monument" title="Welsford-Parker Monument">Welsford-Parker Monument</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Halifax_Regional_Municipality" title="Halifax Regional Municipality">Halifax, Nova Scotia</a> – the only <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a> monument in North America</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Nova Scotians fought in the <a href="/wiki/Crimean_War" title="Crimean War">Crimean War</a> of 1853–1856.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MagocsiOntario1999poiujm_29-0"><a href="#cite_note-MagocsiOntario1999poiujm-29">[29]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Welsford-Parker_Monument" title="Welsford-Parker Monument">Welsford-Parker Monument</a> in Halifax is the second-oldest war monument in Canada (1860) and the only Crimean War monument in North America. It commemorates the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Siege_of_Sevastopol_(1854%E2%80%931855)" title="Siege of Sevastopol (1854–1855)">Siege of Sevastopol (1854–1855)</a>.</p>
<p>Thousands of Nova Scotians fought in the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> (1861–1865), primarily on behalf of the <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">North</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Marquis.2C_Greg_1998_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Marquis.2C_Greg_1998-30">[30]</a></sup> The British Empire (including Nova Scotia) <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/British_proclamation_of_neutrality_in_the_American_Civil_War" title="s:British proclamation of neutrality in the American Civil War">declared itself neutral</a> in the conflict. As a result, Britain (and Nova Scotia) continued to trade with both the <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">South</a> and the North. Nova Scotia's economy boomed during the Civil War.</p>
<p>Soon after the American Civil War, Pro-Canadian Confederation <a href="/wiki/List_of_premiers_of_Nova_Scotia" title="List of premiers of Nova Scotia">premier</a> <a href="/wiki/Charles_Tupper" title="Charles Tupper">Charles Tupper</a> led Nova Scotia into the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Confederation" title="Canadian Confederation">Canadian Confederation</a> on July 1, 1867, along with New Brunswick and the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Canada" title="Province of Canada">Province of Canada</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Anti-Confederation_Party" title="Anti-Confederation Party">Anti-Confederation Party</a> was led by <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Howe" title="Joseph Howe">Joseph Howe</a>. Almost three months later, in the election of September 18, 1867, the Anti-Confederation Party won 18 out of 19 federal seats, and 36 out of 38 seats in the provincial legislature.</p>
<p>Nova Scotia became a world leader in both building and owning wooden sailing ships in the second half of the 19th century. Nova Scotia produced internationally recognized shipbuilders <a href="/wiki/Donald_McKay" title="Donald McKay">Donald McKay</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_Dawson_Lawrence" title="William Dawson Lawrence">William Dawson Lawrence</a>. The fame Nova Scotia achieved from sailors was assured when <a href="/wiki/Joshua_Slocum" title="Joshua Slocum">Joshua Slocum</a> became the first man to sail single-handedly around the world (1895). International attention continued into the following century with the many racing victories of the <i><a href="/wiki/Bluenose" title="Bluenose">Bluenose</a></i> schooner. Nova Scotia was also the birthplace and home of <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Cunard" title="Samuel Cunard">Samuel Cunard</a>, a <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">British</a> shipping magnate (born at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Halifax_(former_city)" title="Halifax (former city)">Halifax</a>, Nova Scotia) who founded the <a href="/wiki/Cunard_Line" title="Cunard Line">Cunard Line</a>.</p>
<p>Throughout the 19th century, numerous <a href="/wiki/Business" title="Business">businesses</a> developed in Nova Scotia became of pan-Canadian and international importance: the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Starr_Manufacturing_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Starr Manufacturing Company (page does not exist)">Starr Manufacturing Company</a> (first skate-manufacturer in Canada), the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bank_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Bank of Nova Scotia">Bank of Nova Scotia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cunard_Line" title="Cunard Line">Cunard Line</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Keith%27s_Brewery" title="Alexander Keith's Brewery">Alexander Keith's Brewery</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Morse%27s_Tea_Company&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Morse's Tea Company (page does not exist)">Morse's Tea Company</a> (first tea company in Canada), among others. (Early in the 20th century <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sobey%27s" title="Sobey's">Sobey's</a> was established, as was <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Life" title="Maritime Life">Maritime Life</a>.)</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_origins">Ethnic origins</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Ethnic origins">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>According to the 2006 Canadian census<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> the largest ethnic group in Nova Scotia is <a href="/wiki/Scottish_people" title="Scottish people">Scottish</a> (31.9%), followed by <a href="/wiki/English_people" title="English people">English</a> (31.8%), <a href="/wiki/Irish_people" title="Irish people">Irish</a> (21.6%), <a href="/wiki/French_people" title="French people">French</a> (17.9%), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_people" title="German people">German</a> (11.3%), <a href="/wiki/First_Nations" title="First Nations">Aboriginal origin</a> (5.3%), <a href="/wiki/Dutch_people" title="Dutch people">Dutch</a> (4.1%), <a href="/wiki/Black_Nova_Scotians" title="Black Nova Scotians">Black Canadians</a> (2.8%), <a href="/wiki/Welsh_people" title="Welsh people">Welsh</a> (1.9%) <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Italian_people" title="Italian people">Italian</a> (1.5%), and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Scandinavian_people" title="Scandinavian people">Scandinavian</a> (1.4%). 40.9% of respondents identified their ethnicity as "Canadian".</p>
<p>Nova Scotia has a long history of social justice work to address issues such as racism and sexism within its borders. The <a href="/wiki/Province_House_(Nova_Scotia)" title="Province House (Nova Scotia)">Nova Scotia legislature</a> was the third in Canada to pass <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Canada" title="Human rights in Canada">human rights legislation</a> (1963). The <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_Human_Rights_Commission" title="Nova Scotia Human Rights Commission">Nova Scotia Human Rights Commission</a> was established in 1967.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Maritimer_English" title="Maritimer English">Maritimer English</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_English" title="Cape Breton English">Cape Breton English</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acadian_French" title="Acadian French">Acadian French</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Gaelic" title="Canadian Gaelic">Canadian Gaelic</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Nouvelle-Ecosse_langues.png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2011" data-file-width="1500" height="402" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Nouvelle-Ecosse_langues.png/300px-Nouvelle-Ecosse_langues.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Nouvelle-Ecosse_langues.png/450px-Nouvelle-Ecosse_langues.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/44/Nouvelle-Ecosse_langues.png/600px-Nouvelle-Ecosse_langues.png 2x" width="300"/></a>

</div>
</div>
