<p>Figures shown are for the number of single language responses and the percentage of total single-language responses.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>Nova Scotia is home to the largest Scottish Gaelic speaking community outside of Scotland, with a small number of native speakers in Pictou County, Antigonish County, and Cape Breton Island, and is taught in a number of secondary schools throughout the province.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1871, the largest religious denominations were Protestant with 103,500 (27%); Roman Catholic with 102,000 (26%); Baptist with 73,295 (19%); Anglican with 55,124 (14%); Methodist with 40,748 (10%), Lutheran with 4,958 (1.3%); and Congregationalist with 2,538 (0.65%).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup></p>
<p>According to the 2001 census, the largest denominations by number of adherents were the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic Church</a> with 327,940 (37%); the <a href="/wiki/United_Church_of_Canada" title="United Church of Canada">United Church of Canada</a> with 142,520 (17%); and the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Church_of_Canada" title="Anglican Church of Canada">Anglican Church of Canada</a> with 120,315 (13%).There are also 8,505 (0.9%) Muslims according to 2011 census.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:YarmouthNS_FishingBoats.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1371" data-file-width="2048" height="114" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/YarmouthNS_FishingBoats.jpg/170px-YarmouthNS_FishingBoats.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/YarmouthNS_FishingBoats.jpg/255px-YarmouthNS_FishingBoats.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/YarmouthNS_FishingBoats.jpg/340px-YarmouthNS_FishingBoats.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:YarmouthNS_FishingBoats.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lobster fishing boats in <a href="/wiki/Yarmouth,_Nova_Scotia" title="Yarmouth, Nova Scotia">Yarmouth, Nova Scotia</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Nova Scotia's <a href="/wiki/List_of_Canadian_provinces_and_territories_by_gross_domestic_product" title="List of Canadian provinces and territories by gross domestic product">per capita GDP</a> in 2010 was $38,475, significantly lower than the national average per capita GDP of $47,605 and a little more than half of Canada's richest province, <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a>. GDP growth has lagged behind the rest of the country for at least the past decade.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>Nova Scotia's traditionally <a href="/wiki/Natural_resource" title="Natural resource">resource-based economy</a> has diversified in recent decades. The rise of Nova Scotia as a viable jurisdiction in North America, historically, was driven by the ready availability of natural resources, especially the <a href="/wiki/Fish_stock" title="Fish stock">fish stocks</a> off the <a href="/wiki/Scotian_Shelf" title="Scotian Shelf">Scotian Shelf</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Fishing" title="Fishing">fishery</a> was a pillar of the economy since its development as part of <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a> in the 17th century; however, the fishery suffered a sharp decline due to <a href="/wiki/Overfishing" title="Overfishing">overfishing</a> in the late 20th century. The collapse of the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_Cod" title="Atlantic Cod">cod stocks</a> and the closure of this sector resulted in a loss of approximately 20,000 jobs in 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup> Other sectors in the province were also hit hard, particularly during the last two decades: coal mining in Cape Breton and northern mainland Nova Scotia has virtually ceased production, and a <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Steel_Corporation" title="Sydney Steel Corporation">large steel</a> mill in <a href="/wiki/Sydney,_Nova_Scotia" title="Sydney, Nova Scotia">Sydney</a> closed during the 1990s. More recently, the high value of the Canadian dollar relative to the US dollar has hurt the forestry industry, leading to the shut down of a long-running <a href="/wiki/Bowater_Mersey_Paper_Company_Limited" title="Bowater Mersey Paper Company Limited">pulp and paper mill</a> near <a href="/wiki/Liverpool,_Nova_Scotia" title="Liverpool, Nova Scotia">Liverpool</a>. Mining, especially of <a href="/wiki/Gypsum" title="Gypsum">gypsum</a> and salt and to a lesser extent <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Silica" title="Silica">silica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peat" title="Peat">peat</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barite" title="Barite">barite</a>, is also a significant sector.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> Since 1991, <a href="/wiki/Offshore_drilling" title="Offshore drilling">offshore oil and gas</a> has become an increasingly important part of the economy, although production and revenue are now declining.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-autogenerated1_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-autogenerated1-41">[41]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">Agriculture</a> remains an important sector in the province, particularly in the <a href="/wiki/Annapolis_Valley" title="Annapolis Valley">Annapolis Valley</a>.</p>
<p>Nova Scotia’s defence and aerospace sector generates approximately $500 million in revenues and contributes about $1.5 billion to the provincial economy annually.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Grafton,_Nova_Scotia.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="3264" data-file-width="4912" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Grafton%2C_Nova_Scotia.JPG/220px-Grafton%2C_Nova_Scotia.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Grafton%2C_Nova_Scotia.JPG/330px-Grafton%2C_Nova_Scotia.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/Grafton%2C_Nova_Scotia.JPG/440px-Grafton%2C_Nova_Scotia.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Grafton,_Nova_Scotia.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Corn growing at <a href="/wiki/Grafton,_Nova_Scotia" title="Grafton, Nova Scotia">Grafton</a> in the Annapolis Valley in October 2011</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> To date, 40% of Canada’s military assets reside in Nova Scotia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Nova Scotia has the fourth-largest <a href="/wiki/Film_industry" title="Film industry">film industry</a> in Canada hosting over 100 productions yearly, more than half of which are the products of international film and television producers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> In 2015, the government of Nova Scotia eliminated tax credits to film production in the province, jeopardizing the industry given most other jurisdictions continue to offer such credits.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup></p>
<p>The Nova Scotia <a href="/wiki/Tourism" title="Tourism">tourism</a> industry includes more than 6,500 direct businesses, supporting nearly 40,000 jobs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> 200,000 <a href="/wiki/Cruise_ship" title="Cruise ship">cruise ship</a> passengers from around the world flow through the <a href="/wiki/Port_of_Halifax" title="Port of Halifax">Port of Halifax</a>, Nova Scotia each year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-gov-ns1_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-gov-ns1-49">[49]</a></sup> This industry contributes approximately $1.3 billion annually to the economy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> The province also boasts a rapidly developing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Information_Technology" title="Information Technology">Information &amp; Communication Technology</a> (ICT) sector which consists of over 500 companies, and employs roughly 15,000 people.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup> In 2006, the manufacturing sector brought in over $2.6 billion in chained GDP, the largest output of any industrial sector in Nova Scotia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Michelin" title="Michelin">Michelin</a> remains by far the largest single employer in this sector, operating three production plants in the province.</p>
<p>As of 2012, the median family income in Nova Scotia was $67,910, below the national average of $74,540;<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> in Halifax the figure rises to $80,490.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:652px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Hall%27s_Harbour,_Nova_Scotia.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1856" data-file-width="8192" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Hall%27s_Harbour%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg/650px-Hall%27s_Harbour%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Hall%27s_Harbour%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg/975px-Hall%27s_Harbour%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0e/Hall%27s_Harbour%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg/1300px-Hall%27s_Harbour%2C_Nova_Scotia.jpg 2x" width="650"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Hall%27s_Harbour,_Nova_Scotia.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The fishing boats are completely aground at low tide along the rich fishing grounds of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Fundy_Bay" title="Fundy Bay">Fundy Bay</a>, at <a href="/wiki/Hall%27s_Harbour,_Nova_Scotia" title="Hall's Harbour, Nova Scotia">Hall's Harbour, Nova Scotia</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The province is the world’s largest exporter of <a href="/wiki/Christmas_tree" title="Christmas tree">Christmas trees</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lobster" title="Lobster">lobster</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gypsum" title="Gypsum">gypsum</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Berry" title="Berry">wild berries</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> Its export value of fish exceeds $1 billion, and fish products are received by 90 countries around the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> Nevertheless, the province's imports far exceed its exports. While these numbers were roughly equal from 1992 until 2004, since that time the trade deficit has ballooned. In 2012, exports from Nova Scotia were 12.1% of provincial GDP, while imports were 22.6%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span id="Government,_law_and_politics"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Government.2C_law_and_politics">Government, law and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Government, law and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Government_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Government of Nova Scotia">Government of Nova Scotia</a> and <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Politics of Nova Scotia">Politics of Nova Scotia</a></div>
<p>Nova Scotia is ordered by a <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary government</a> within the construct of <a href="/wiki/Constitutional_monarchy" title="Constitutional monarchy">constitutional monarchy</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_in_Nova_Scotia" title="Monarchy in Nova Scotia">monarchy in Nova Scotia</a> is the foundation of the <a href="/wiki/Executive_(government)" title="Executive (government)">executive</a>, <a href="/wiki/Legislature" title="Legislature">legislative</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Judiciary" title="Judiciary">judicial</a> branches.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> The sovereign is Queen <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_II" title="Elizabeth II">Elizabeth II</a>, who also serves as head of state of <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_realm" title="Commonwealth realm">15 other Commonwealth countries</a>, each of Canada's nine other provinces, and the Canadian federal realm, and resides predominantly in the United Kingdom. As such, the Queen's representative, the <a href="/wiki/Lieutenant_Governor_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Lieutenant Governor of Nova Scotia">Lieutenant Governor of Nova Scotia</a> (presently <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Arthur_Joseph_LeBlanc" title="Arthur Joseph LeBlanc">Arthur Joseph LeBlanc</a> ), carries out most of the royal duties in Nova Scotia.</p>
<p>In 1937, <a href="/wiki/Everett_Farmer" title="Everett Farmer">Everett Farmer</a> was the last person hanged (for murder) in Nova Scotia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nscourts_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-nscourts-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Halifaxnighttime.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1800" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Halifaxnighttime.jpg/220px-Halifaxnighttime.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Halifaxnighttime.jpg/330px-Halifaxnighttime.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c1/Halifaxnighttime.jpg/440px-Halifaxnighttime.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Halifaxnighttime.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Halifax, the provincial capital</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The direct participation of the royal and viceroyal figures in any of these areas of governance is limited, though; in practice, their use of the executive powers is directed by <a href="/wiki/Executive_Council_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Executive Council of Nova Scotia">the Executive Council</a>, a committee of <a href="/wiki/Minister_of_the_Crown" title="Minister of the Crown">ministers of the Crown</a> responsible to the unicameral, elected <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_House_of_Assembly" title="Nova Scotia House of Assembly">House of Assembly</a> and chosen and headed by the <a href="/wiki/Premier_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Premier of Nova Scotia">Premier of Nova Scotia</a> (presently <a href="/wiki/Stephen_McNeil" title="Stephen McNeil">Stephen McNeil</a>), the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. To ensure the stability of government, the lieutenant governor will usually appoint as premier the person who is the current leader of the political party that can obtain the confidence of a <a href="/wiki/Plurality_(voting)" title="Plurality (voting)">plurality</a> in the House of Assembly. The leader of the party with the second-most seats usually becomes the <a href="/wiki/Leader_of_the_Opposition_(Nova_Scotia)" title="Leader of the Opposition (Nova Scotia)">Leader of Her Majesty's Loyal Opposition</a> (presently <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Baillie" title="Jamie Baillie">Jamie Baillie</a>) and is part of an adversarial parliamentary system intended to keep the government in check.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>Each of the 51 <a href="/wiki/Member_of_the_Legislative_Assembly" title="Member of the Legislative Assembly">Members of the Legislative Assembly</a> in the House of Assembly is elected by single member plurality in an <a href="/wiki/Electoral_district_(Canada)" title="Electoral district (Canada)">electoral district</a> or riding. General elections must be called by the lieutenant governor on the advice of the premier, or may be triggered by the government losing a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Confidence_vote" title="Confidence vote">confidence vote</a> in the House.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> There are three dominant political parties in Nova Scotia: the <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_Liberal_Party" title="Nova Scotia Liberal Party">Liberal Party</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_New_Democratic_Party" title="Nova Scotia New Democratic Party">New Democratic Party</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Progressive_Conservative_Association_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Progressive Conservative Association of Nova Scotia">Progressive Conservative Party</a>. The other two registered parties are the <a href="/wiki/Green_Party_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Green Party of Nova Scotia">Green Party of Nova Scotia</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantica_Party" title="Atlantica Party">Atlantica Party</a>, neither of which has a seat in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Assembly" title="House of Assembly">House of Assembly</a>.</p>
<p>The province's revenue comes mainly from the taxation of personal and corporate income, although taxes on tobacco and alcohol, its stake in the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Lottery_Corporation" title="Atlantic Lottery Corporation">Atlantic Lottery Corporation</a>, and oil and gas royalties are also significant. In 2006–07, the province passed a budget of $6.9 billion, with a projected $72 million surplus. Federal equalization payments account for $1.385 billion, or 20.07% of the provincial revenue. The province participates in the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harmonized_Sales_Tax" title="Harmonized Sales Tax">HST</a>, a blended sales tax collected by the federal government using the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Goods_and_Services_Tax_(Canada)" title="Goods and Services Tax (Canada)">GST</a> tax system.</p>
<p>Nova Scotia no longer has any incorporated cities; they were amalgamated into <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Regional_Municipality" title="Regional Municipality">Regional Municipalities</a> in 1996.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture<span id="Culture"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fine_arts">Fine arts</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Fine arts">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:HectorPioneerByJohnWilson.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="418" data-file-width="291" height="244" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/HectorPioneerByJohnWilson.jpg/170px-HectorPioneerByJohnWilson.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/HectorPioneerByJohnWilson.jpg/255px-HectorPioneerByJohnWilson.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/cb/HectorPioneerByJohnWilson.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:HectorPioneerByJohnWilson.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Hector_(ship)" title="Hector (ship)">Hector Pioneer</a> by Nova Scotian sculptor <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Wilson_(sculptor)" title="John Wilson (sculptor)">John Wilson</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pictou,_Nova_Scotia" title="Pictou, Nova Scotia">Pictou, Nova Scotia</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Nova Scotia has long been a centre for artistic and cultural excellence. The capital, Halifax, hosts institutions such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_College_of_Art_and_Design_University" title="Nova Scotia College of Art and Design University">Nova Scotia College of Art and Design University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Art_Gallery_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Art Gallery of Nova Scotia">Art Gallery of Nova Scotia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neptune_Theatre_(Halifax)" title="Neptune Theatre (Halifax)">Neptune Theatre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dalhousie_Arts_Centre" title="Dalhousie Arts Centre">Dalhousie Arts Centre</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Two_Planks_and_a_Passion_Theatre&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Two Planks and a Passion Theatre (page does not exist)">Two Planks and a Passion Theatre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ship%27s_Company_Theatre" title="Ship's Company Theatre">Ship's Company Theatre</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Symphony_Nova_Scotia" title="Symphony Nova Scotia">Symphony Nova Scotia</a>. The province is home to avant-garde visual art and traditional crafting, writing and publishing and a film industry.</p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:WelsfordParkerMonumentHalifaxNSCanada.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1936" data-file-width="2592" height="127" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/WelsfordParkerMonumentHalifaxNSCanada.JPG/170px-WelsfordParkerMonumentHalifaxNSCanada.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/WelsfordParkerMonumentHalifaxNSCanada.JPG/255px-WelsfordParkerMonumentHalifaxNSCanada.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/20/WelsfordParkerMonumentHalifaxNSCanada.JPG/340px-WelsfordParkerMonumentHalifaxNSCanada.JPG 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:WelsfordParkerMonumentHalifaxNSCanada.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Lion carved by <a href="/wiki/George_Lang_(builder)" title="George Lang (builder)">George Lang</a>, <a href="/wiki/Welsford-Parker_Monument" title="Welsford-Parker Monument">Welsford-Parker Monument</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Much of the historic public art sculptures in the province were made by New York sculptor <a href="/wiki/J._Massey_Rhind" title="J. Massey Rhind">J. Massey Rhind</a> as well as Canadian sculptors <a href="/wiki/Hamilton_MacCarthy" title="Hamilton MacCarthy">Hamilton MacCarthy</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_William_Hill_(sculptor)" title="George William Hill (sculptor)">George Hill</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emanuel_Hahn" title="Emanuel Hahn">Emanuel Hahn</a> and <a href="/wiki/Louis-Philippe_H%C3%A9bert" title="Louis-Philippe Hébert">Louis-Philippe Hébert</a>. Some of this public art was also created by Nova Scotian <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Wilson_(sculptor)" title="John Wilson (sculptor)">John Wilson (sculptor)</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> Nova Scotian <a href="/wiki/George_Lang_(builder)" title="George Lang (builder)">George Lang</a> was a <a href="/wiki/Stone_sculpture" title="Stone sculpture">stone sculptor</a> who also built many landmark buildings in the province, including the <a href="/wiki/Welsford-Parker_Monument" title="Welsford-Parker Monument">Welsford-Parker Monument</a>.</p>
<p>Some of the province's greatest painters were <a href="/wiki/William_Valentine_(painter)" title="William Valentine (painter)">William Valentine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maria_Frances_Ann_Morris" title="Maria Frances Ann Morris">Maria Morris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jack_L._Gray" title="Jack L. Gray">Jack L. Gray</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mabel_Killiam_Day&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mabel Killiam Day (page does not exist)">Mabel Killiam Day</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Lawson" title="Ernest Lawson">Ernest Lawson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Frances_Bannerman" title="Frances Bannerman">Frances Bannerman</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alex_Colville" title="Alex Colville">Alex Colville</a>, <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tom_Forrestall&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tom Forrestall (page does not exist)">Tom Forrestall</a> and ship portrait artist <a href="/wiki/John_O%27Brien_(marine_artist)" title="John O'Brien (marine artist)">John O'Brien</a>. Some of most notable artists whose works have been acquired by Nova Scotia are British artist <a href="/wiki/Joshua_Reynolds" title="Joshua Reynolds">Joshua Reynolds</a> (collection of Art Gallery of Nova Scotia); <a href="/wiki/William_Gush" title="William Gush">William Gush</a> and <a href="/wiki/William_J._Weaver" title="William J. Weaver">William J. Weaver</a> (both have works in <a href="/wiki/Province_House_(Nova_Scotia)" title="Province House (Nova Scotia)">Province House</a>); <a href="/wiki/Robert_Field_(painter)" title="Robert Field (painter)">Robert Field</a> (<a href="/wiki/Government_House_(Nova_Scotia)" title="Government House (Nova Scotia)">Government House</a>), as well as leading American artists <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_West" title="Benjamin West">Benjamin West</a> (self portrait in <a href="/wiki/The_Halifax_Club" title="The Halifax Club">The Halifax Club</a>, portrait of chief justice in <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_Supreme_Court" title="Nova Scotia Supreme Court">Nova Scotia Supreme Court</a>), <a href="/wiki/John_Singleton_Copley" title="John Singleton Copley">John Singleton Copley</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robert_Feke" title="Robert Feke">Robert Feke</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Robert_Field_(painter)" title="Robert Field (painter)">Robert Field</a> (the latter three have works in the <a href="/wiki/Richard_John_Uniacke" title="Richard John Uniacke">Uniacke Estate</a>).</p>
<p>Two famous Nova Scotian photographers are <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Wallace_R._MacAskill&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Wallace R. MacAskill (page does not exist)">Wallace R. MacAskill</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sherman_Hines" title="Sherman Hines">Sherman Hines</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> Three of the most accomplished illustrators were <a href="/wiki/George_Wylie_Hutchinson" title="George Wylie Hutchinson">George Wylie Hutchinson</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bob_Chambers_(cartoonist)" title="Bob Chambers (cartoonist)">Bob Chambers (cartoonist)</a> and <a href="/wiki/Donald_A._Mackay" title="Donald A. Mackay">Donald A. Mackay</a>.</p>
<p>Renowned american artists like sculptor <a href="/wiki/Richard_Serra" title="Richard Serra">Richard Serra</a>, composer <a href="/wiki/Philip_Glass" title="Philip Glass">Philip Glass</a> and abstract painter <a href="/wiki/John_Beardman" title="John Beardman">John Beardman</a> spent part of the year in Nova Scotia.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Film_and_television">Film and television</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Film and television">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Nova_Scotia" title="List of people from Nova Scotia">Actors and filmmakers in Nova Scotia</a></div>
<p>Nova Scotia has produced numerous film actors. <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> nominee <a href="/wiki/Ellen_Page" title="Ellen Page">Ellen Page</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Juno_(film)" title="Juno (film)">Juno</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Inception" title="Inception">Inception</a></i>) was born in Halifax, Nova Scotia; five-time <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> nominee <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Kennedy" title="Arthur Kennedy">Arthur Kennedy</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Lawrence_of_Arabia_(film)" title="Lawrence of Arabia (film)">Lawrence of Arabia</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/High_Sierra_(film)" title="High Sierra (film)">High Sierra</a></i>) called Nova Scotia his home; and two time <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Globe" title="Golden Globe">Golden Globe</a> winner <a href="/wiki/Donald_Sutherland" title="Donald Sutherland">Donald Sutherland</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/MASH_(film)" title="MASH (film)">MASH</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Ordinary_People" title="Ordinary People">Ordinary People</a></i>) spent most of his youth in the province. Other actors include <a href="/wiki/John_Paul_Tremblay" title="John Paul Tremblay">John Paul Tremblay</a>, <a href="/wiki/Robb_Wells" title="Robb Wells">Robb Wells</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mike_Smith_(actor)" title="Mike Smith (actor)">Mike Smith</a> and <a href="/wiki/John_Dunsworth" title="John Dunsworth">John Dunsworth</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Trailer_Park_Boys" title="Trailer Park Boys">Trailer Park Boys</a></i> and actress <a href="/wiki/Joanne_Kelly" title="Joanne Kelly">Joanne Kelly</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Warehouse_13" title="Warehouse 13">Warehouse 13</a></i>.</p>
<p>Nova Scotia has also produced numerous film directors such as <a href="/wiki/Thom_Fitzgerald" title="Thom Fitzgerald">Thom Fitzgerald</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Hanging_Garden_(film)" title="The Hanging Garden (film)">The Hanging Garden</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Petrie" title="Daniel Petrie">Daniel Petrie</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Resurrection_(1980_film)" title="Resurrection (1980 film)">Resurrection</a></i>—Academy Award nominee) and Acadian film director <a href="/wiki/Phil_Comeau" title="Phil Comeau">Phil Comeau</a>'s multiple award-winning local story (<i><a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Le_secret_de_J%C3%A9r%C3%B4me_(film)&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Le secret de Jérôme (film) (page does not exist)">Le secret de Jérôme</a></i>).</p>
<p>Nova Scotian stories are the subject of numerous feature films: <i><a href="/wiki/Margaret%27s_Museum" title="Margaret's Museum">Margaret's Museum</a></i> (starring <a href="/wiki/Helena_Bonham_Carter" title="Helena Bonham Carter">Helena Bonham Carter</a>); <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bay_Boy" title="The Bay Boy">The Bay Boy</a></i> (directed by <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Petrie" title="Daniel Petrie">Daniel Petrie</a> and starring <a href="/wiki/Kiefer_Sutherland" title="Kiefer Sutherland">Kiefer Sutherland</a>); <i><a href="/wiki/New_Waterford_Girl" title="New Waterford Girl">New Waterford Girl</a></i>; <i><a href="/wiki/The_Story_of_Adele_H." title="The Story of Adele H.">The Story of Adele H.</a></i> (the story of unrequited love of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Adele_Hugo" title="Adele Hugo">Adele Hugo</a>); and two films of <i>Evangeline</i> (one starring <a href="/wiki/Miriam_Cooper" title="Miriam Cooper">Miriam Cooper</a> and another starring <a href="/wiki/Dolores_del_R%C3%ADo" title="Dolores del Río">Dolores del Río</a>).</p>
<p>There is a significant film industry in Nova Scotia. Feature filmmaking began in Canada with <i>Evangeline</i> (1913), made by <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Bioscope_Company" title="Canadian Bioscope Company">Canadian Bioscope Company</a> in Halifax, which released six films before it closed. The film has since been lost. Some of the award-winning feature films made in the province are <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i> (starring <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_DiCaprio" title="Leonardo DiCaprio">Leonardo DiCaprio</a> and <a href="/wiki/Kate_Winslet" title="Kate Winslet">Kate Winslet</a>); <i><a href="/wiki/The_Shipping_News" title="The Shipping News">The Shipping News</a></i> (starring <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Spacey" title="Kevin Spacey">Kevin Spacey</a> and <a href="/wiki/Julianne_Moore" title="Julianne Moore">Julianne Moore</a>); <i><a href="/wiki/K-19:_The_Widowmaker" title="K-19: The Widowmaker">K-19: The Widowmaker</a></i> (starring <a href="/wiki/Harrison_Ford" title="Harrison Ford">Harrison Ford</a> and <a href="/wiki/Liam_Neeson" title="Liam Neeson">Liam Neeson</a>) and <i><a href="/wiki/Amelia_(film)" title="Amelia (film)">Amelia</a></i> (starring <a href="/wiki/Hilary_Swank" title="Hilary Swank">Hilary Swank</a>, <a href="/wiki/Richard_Gere" title="Richard Gere">Richard Gere</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ewan_McGregor" title="Ewan McGregor">Ewan McGregor</a>).</p>
<p>Nova Scotia has also produced numerous television series: <i><a href="/wiki/This_Hour_Has_22_Minutes" title="This Hour Has 22 Minutes">This Hour Has 22 Minutes</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Don_Messer%27s_Jubilee" title="Don Messer's Jubilee">Don Messer's Jubilee</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Harbour" title="Black Harbour">Black Harbour</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Haven_(TV_series)" title="Haven (TV series)">Haven</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Trailer_Park_Boys" title="Trailer Park Boys">Trailer Park Boys</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mr._D" title="Mr. D">Mr. D</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Call_Me_Fitz" title="Call Me Fitz">Call Me Fitz</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Theodore_Tugboat" title="Theodore Tugboat">Theodore Tugboat</a></i>. The <i><a href="/wiki/Jesse_Stone_(character)" title="Jesse Stone (character)">Jesse Stone</a></i> film series on <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">CBS</a> starring <a href="/wiki/Tom_Selleck" title="Tom Selleck">Tom Selleck</a> is also routinely produced in the province.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Literature">Literature</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Literature">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Nova_Scotia" title="List of people from Nova Scotia">Writers in Nova Scotia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sailing-Alone-Around-the-World-cover.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1128" data-file-width="733" height="262" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Sailing-Alone-Around-the-World-cover.jpg/170px-Sailing-Alone-Around-the-World-cover.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Sailing-Alone-Around-the-World-cover.jpg/255px-Sailing-Alone-Around-the-World-cover.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9e/Sailing-Alone-Around-the-World-cover.jpg/340px-Sailing-Alone-Around-the-World-cover.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sailing-Alone-Around-the-World-cover.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Original cover 1900</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are numerous Nova Scotian authors who have achieved international fame: <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Chandler_Haliburton" title="Thomas Chandler Haliburton">Thomas Chandler Haliburton</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Sam_Slick" title="Sam Slick">The Clockmaker</a></i>); <a href="/wiki/Alistair_MacLeod" title="Alistair MacLeod">Alistair MacLeod</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/No_Great_Mischief" title="No Great Mischief">No Great Mischief</a></i>); <a href="/wiki/Margaret_Marshall_Saunders" title="Margaret Marshall Saunders">Margaret Marshall Saunders</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Beautiful_Joe" title="Beautiful Joe">Beautiful Joe</a></i>), <a href="/wiki/Laurence_Bradford_Dakin" title="Laurence Bradford Dakin">Laurence B. Dakin</a> (Marco Polo), and <a href="/wiki/Joshua_Slocum" title="Joshua Slocum">Joshua Slocum</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Sailing_Alone_Around_the_World" title="Sailing Alone Around the World">Sailing Alone Around the World</a></i>). Other authors include <a href="/wiki/Johanna_Skibsrud" title="Johanna Skibsrud">Johanna Skibsrud</a> (<i>The Sentimentalists</i>), <a href="/wiki/Alden_Nowlan" title="Alden Nowlan">Alden Nowlan</a> (<i>Bread, Wine and Salt</i>), <a href="/wiki/George_Elliott_Clarke" title="George Elliott Clarke">George Elliott Clarke</a> (<i>Execution Poems</i>), <a href="/wiki/Lesley_Choyce" title="Lesley Choyce">Lesley Choyce</a> (<i>Nova Scotia: Shaped by the Sea</i>), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thomas_Raddall" title="Thomas Raddall">Thomas Raddall</a> (<i>Halifax: Warden of the North</i>), <a href="/wiki/Donna_Morrissey" title="Donna Morrissey">Donna Morrissey</a> (<i>Kit's Law</i>), <a href="/wiki/Frank_Parker_Day" title="Frank Parker Day">Frank Parker Day</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Rockbound" title="Rockbound">Rockbound</a></i>).</p>
<p>Nova Scotia has also been the subject of numerous literary books. Some of the international best-sellers are: <i>Last Man Out: The Story of the Springhill Mining Disaster</i> (by <a href="/wiki/Melissa_Fay_Greene" title="Melissa Fay Greene">Melissa Fay Greene</a>) ; <i>Curse of the Narrows: The <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Explosion" title="Halifax Explosion">Halifax Explosion</a> 1917</i> (by Laura MacDonald); "In the Village" (short story by <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a>–winning author <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Bishop" title="Elizabeth Bishop">Elizabeth Bishop</a>); and <a href="/wiki/National_Book_Critics_Circle_Award" title="National Book Critics Circle Award">National Book Critics Circle Award</a> winner <i><a href="/wiki/Rough_Crossings" title="Rough Crossings">Rough Crossings</a></i> (by <a href="/wiki/Simon_Schama" title="Simon Schama">Simon Schama</a>). Other authors who have written novels about Nova Scotian stories include: <a href="/wiki/Linden_MacIntyre" title="Linden MacIntyre">Linden MacIntyre</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Bishop%27s_Man" title="The Bishop's Man">The Bishop's Man</a></i>); <a href="/wiki/Hugh_MacLennan" title="Hugh MacLennan">Hugh MacLennan</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Barometer_Rising" title="Barometer Rising">Barometer Rising</a></i>); <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Buckler" title="Ernest Buckler">Ernest Buckler</a> (<i>The Valley and the Mountain</i>); <a href="/wiki/Archibald_MacMechan" title="Archibald MacMechan">Archibald MacMechan</a> (<i>Red Snow on Grand Pré</i>), <a href="/wiki/Henry_Wadsworth_Longfellow" title="Henry Wadsworth Longfellow">Henry Wadsworth Longfellow</a> (long poem <i><a href="/wiki/Evangeline" title="Evangeline">Evangeline</a></i>); <a href="/wiki/Lawrence_Hill" title="Lawrence Hill">Lawrence Hill</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/The_Book_of_Negroes_(novel)" title="The Book of Negroes (novel)">The Book of Negroes</a></i>) and <a href="/wiki/John_Mack_Faragher" title="John Mack Faragher">John Mack Faragher</a> (<i>Great and Nobel Scheme</i>).</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Nova_Scotia" title="Music of Nova Scotia">Music of Nova Scotia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MamasAndPapas260.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="304" data-file-width="260" height="199" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/MamasAndPapas260.jpg/170px-MamasAndPapas260.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/9e/MamasAndPapas260.jpg/255px-MamasAndPapas260.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/9/9e/MamasAndPapas260.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MamasAndPapas260.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Denny_Doherty" title="Denny Doherty">Denny Doherty</a> (left) of <a href="/wiki/The_Mamas_%26_the_Papas" title="The Mamas &amp; the Papas">The Mamas &amp; the Papas</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Nova Scotia has produced numerous musicians. The <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> winners include <a href="/wiki/Denny_Doherty" title="Denny Doherty">Denny Doherty</a> (from <a href="/wiki/The_Mamas_%26_the_Papas" title="The Mamas &amp; the Papas">The Mamas &amp; the Papas</a>), <a href="/wiki/Anne_Murray" title="Anne Murray">Anne Murray</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sarah_McLachlan" title="Sarah McLachlan">Sarah McLachlan</a>. Other musicians include country singer <a href="/wiki/Hank_Snow" title="Hank Snow">Hank Snow</a>, country singer <a href="/wiki/George_Canyon" title="George Canyon">George Canyon</a>, jazz singer <a href="/wiki/Holly_Cole" title="Holly Cole">Holly Cole</a>, opera singers <a href="/wiki/Portia_White" title="Portia White">Portia White</a> and <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Hannigan" title="Barbara Hannigan">Barbara Hannigan</a>, multi-<a href="/wiki/Juno_Award" title="Juno Award">Juno Award</a> nominated rapper <a href="/wiki/Classified_(rapper)" title="Classified (rapper)">Classified</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rita_MacNeil" title="Rita MacNeil">Rita MacNeil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Matt_Mays" title="Matt Mays">Matt Mays</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sloan_(band)" title="Sloan (band)">Sloan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Feist_(singer)" title="Feist (singer)">Feist</a>, <a href="/wiki/Todd_Fancey" title="Todd Fancey">Todd Fancey</a>, <a href="/wiki/The_Rankin_Family" title="The Rankin Family">The Rankin Family</a>, <a href="/wiki/April_Wine" title="April Wine">April Wine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Buck_65" title="Buck 65">Buck 65</a>, <a href="/wiki/Joel_Plaskett" title="Joel Plaskett">Joel Plaskett</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grand_D%C3%A9rangement_(band)" title="Grand Dérangement (band)">Grand Dérangement</a>, and country music singer <a href="/wiki/Drake_Jensen" title="Drake Jensen">Drake Jensen</a>.</p>
<p>There are numerous songs written about Nova Scotia: The Ballad of Springhill (written by <a href="/wiki/Peggy_Seeger" title="Peggy Seeger">Peggy Seeger</a> and performed by Irish folk singer <a href="/wiki/Luke_Kelly" title="Luke Kelly">Luke Kelly</a> a member of <a href="/wiki/The_Dubliners" title="The Dubliners">The Dubliners</a>, <a href="/wiki/U2" title="U2">U2</a>); numerous songs by <a href="/wiki/Stan_Rogers" title="Stan Rogers">Stan Rogers</a> including Bluenose, The Jeannie C (mentions Little Dover, NS), <a href="/wiki/Barrett%27s_Privateers" title="Barrett's Privateers">Barrett's Privateers</a>, Giant, and The Rawdon Hills; Farewell to Nova Scotia (traditional); Blue Nose (<a href="/wiki/Stompin%27_Tom_Connors" title="Stompin' Tom Connors">Stompin' Tom Connors</a>); She’s Called Nova Scotia (by <a href="/wiki/Rita_MacNeil" title="Rita MacNeil">Rita MacNeil</a>); Cape Breton (by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/David_Myles_(singer-songwriter)" title="David Myles (singer-songwriter)">David Myles</a>); <a href="/wiki/Acadian_Driftwood" title="Acadian Driftwood">Acadian Driftwood</a> (by <a href="/wiki/Robbie_Robertson" title="Robbie Robertson">Robbie Robertson</a>); Acadie (by <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Lanois" title="Daniel Lanois">Daniel Lanois</a>); and My Nova Scotia Home (by <a href="/wiki/Hank_Snow" title="Hank Snow">Hank Snow</a>).</p>
<p>Nova Scotia has also produced some significant songwriters such as <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> winning <a href="/wiki/Gordie_Sampson" title="Gordie Sampson">Gordie Sampson</a>. Sampson has written songs for <a href="/wiki/Carrie_Underwood" title="Carrie Underwood">Carrie Underwood</a> ("Jesus, Take the Wheel", "Just a Dream", "Get Out of This Town"), <a href="/wiki/Martina_McBride" title="Martina McBride">Martina McBride</a> ("If I Had Your Name", You're Not Leavin Me"), <a href="/wiki/LeAnn_Rimes" title="LeAnn Rimes">LeAnn Rimes</a> ("Long Night", "Save Myself"), and <a href="/wiki/George_Canyon" title="George Canyon">George Canyon</a> ("My Name"). Another successful Nova Scotia songwriter was <a href="/wiki/Hank_Snow" title="Hank Snow">Hank Snow</a> whose songs have been recorded by <a href="/wiki/The_Rolling_Stones" title="The Rolling Stones">The Rolling Stones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Elvis_Presley" title="Elvis Presley">Elvis Presley</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Cash" title="Johnny Cash">Johnny Cash</a>.</p>
<p>Music producer <a href="/wiki/Brian_Ahern_(producer)" title="Brian Ahern (producer)">Brian Ahern</a> is a Nova Scotian. He got his start by being music director for CBC television's <a href="/wiki/Singalong_Jubilee" title="Singalong Jubilee">Singalong Jubilee</a>. He later produced 12 albums for <a href="/wiki/Anne_Murray" title="Anne Murray">Anne Murray</a> (“Snowbird,” Danny’s Song” and “You Won’t See Me”); 11 albums for <a href="/wiki/Emmylou_Harris" title="Emmylou Harris">Emmylou Harris</a> (whom he married at his home in Halifax on January 9, 1977).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Brian_Ahern_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-Brian_Ahern-63">[63]</a></sup> He also produced discs for <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Cash" title="Johnny Cash">Johnny Cash</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_Jones" title="George Jones">George Jones</a>, <a href="/wiki/Roy_Orbison" title="Roy Orbison">Roy Orbison</a>, <a href="/wiki/Glen_Campbell" title="Glen Campbell">Glen Campbell</a>, <a href="/wiki/Don_Williams" title="Don Williams">Don Williams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jesse_Winchester" title="Jesse Winchester">Jesse Winchester</a> and <a href="/wiki/Linda_Ronstadt" title="Linda Ronstadt">Linda Ronstadt</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ahern_Allmusic_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ahern_Allmusic-64">[64]</a></sup> Another noted writer is Cape Bretoner <a href="/wiki/Leon_Dubinsky" title="Leon Dubinsky">Leon Dubinsky</a>, who wrote the anthem, "<a href="/wiki/Rise_Again_(The_Rankin_Family_song)" title="Rise Again (The Rankin Family song)">Rise Again</a>", among many other songs performed by various Canadian artists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leon_Dubinsky_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Leon_Dubinsky-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_people_from_Nova_Scotia" title="List of people from Nova Scotia">Sports people in Nova Scotia</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:SidneyCrosby.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="572" data-file-width="551" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/SidneyCrosby.jpg/170px-SidneyCrosby.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/SidneyCrosby.jpg/255px-SidneyCrosby.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2a/SidneyCrosby.jpg/340px-SidneyCrosby.jpg 2x" width="170"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:SidneyCrosby.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Sidney_Crosby" title="Sidney Crosby">Sidney Crosby</a> from <a href="/wiki/Cole_Harbour,_Nova_Scotia" title="Cole Harbour, Nova Scotia">Cole Harbour</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Sport is an important part of Nova Scotia culture. There are numerous semi pro, university and amateur sports teams, for example, The <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Mooseheads" title="Halifax Mooseheads">Halifax Mooseheads</a>, 2013 Canadian Hockey League Memorial Cup Champions, and the <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Screaming_Eagles" title="Cape Breton Screaming Eagles">Cape Breton Screaming Eagles</a>, both of the Quebec Major Junior Hockey League. The <a href="/wiki/Halifax_Hurricanes" title="Halifax Hurricanes">Halifax Hurricanes</a> of the National Basketball League of Canada is another team that calls Nova Scotia home, and were 2016 league champions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_Open" title="Nova Scotia Open">Nova Scotia Open</a> is a professional <a href="/wiki/Golf" title="Golf">golf</a> tournament on the <a href="/wiki/Web.com_Tour" title="Web.com Tour">Web.com Tour</a> since 2014.</p>
<p>The province has also produced numerous athletes such as <a href="/wiki/Sidney_Crosby" title="Sidney Crosby">Sidney Crosby</a> (ice hockey), <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nathan_Mackinnon" title="Nathan Mackinnon">Nathan Mackinnon</a> (ice hockey), <a href="/wiki/Brad_Marchand" title="Brad Marchand">Brad Marchand</a> (ice hockey), <a href="/wiki/Colleen_Jones" title="Colleen Jones">Colleen Jones</a> (curling), <a href="/wiki/Al_MacInnis" title="Al MacInnis">Al MacInnis</a> (ice hockey), <a href="/wiki/TJ_Grant" title="TJ Grant">TJ Grant</a> (mixed martial arts), <a href="/wiki/Rocky_Johnson" title="Rocky Johnson">Rocky Johnson</a> (wrestling, and father of <a href="/wiki/Dwayne_Johnson" title="Dwayne Johnson">Dwayne "The Rock" Johnson</a>), <a href="/wiki/George_Dixon_(boxer)" title="George Dixon (boxer)">George Dixon</a> (boxing) and <a href="/wiki/Kirk_Johnson" title="Kirk Johnson">Kirk Johnson</a> (boxing). The achievements of Nova Scotian athletes are presented at the <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_Sport_Hall_of_Fame" title="Nova Scotia Sport Hall of Fame">Nova Scotia Sport Hall of Fame</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cuisine">Cuisine</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Cuisine">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Cuisine" title="Cuisine">cuisine</a> of Nova Scotia is typically <a href="/wiki/Canadian_cuisine" title="Canadian cuisine">Canadian</a> with an emphasis on local <a href="/wiki/Seafood" title="Seafood">seafood</a>. One endemic dish (in the sense of "peculiar to" and "originating from") is the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Donair" title="Donair">Halifax donair</a>, a distant variant of the <a href="/wiki/Doner_kebab" title="Doner kebab">doner kebab</a> prepared using thinly sliced beef <a href="/wiki/Meatloaf" title="Meatloaf">meatloaf</a> and a sweet <a href="/wiki/Condensed_milk" title="Condensed milk">condensed milk</a> sauce. As well, <a href="/wiki/Hodge-Podge_(soup)" title="Hodge-Podge (soup)">hodge podge</a>, a creamy soup of fresh baby vegetables, is native to Nova Scotia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup></p>
<p>The province is also known for blueberry grunt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Events_and_festivals">Events and festivals</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Events and festivals">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">See also: <a href="/wiki/Category:Festivals_in_Nova_Scotia" title="Category:Festivals in Nova Scotia">Category:Festivals in Nova Scotia</a></div>
<p>There are a number of <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Festivals" title="Festivals">festivals</a> and cultural events that are recurring in Nova Scotia, or notable in its history. The following is an incomplete list of festivals and other cultural gatherings in the province:</p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tourism">Tourism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Tourism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Nova Scotia's tourism industry showcases Nova Scotia's culture, scenery and coastline.</p>
<div class="center">
<div class="thumb tnone">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:652px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Cabot_trail_2009k.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2198" data-file-width="5839" height="245" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Cabot_trail_2009k.JPG/650px-Cabot_trail_2009k.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Cabot_trail_2009k.JPG/975px-Cabot_trail_2009k.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/Cabot_trail_2009k.JPG/1300px-Cabot_trail_2009k.JPG 2x" width="650"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Cabot_trail_2009k.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The <a href="/wiki/Cabot_Trail" title="Cabot Trail">Cabot Trail</a> viewed from the <a href="/wiki/Skyline_Trail_(Cape_Breton_Highlands_National_Park)" title="Skyline Trail (Cape Breton Highlands National Park)">Skyline Hiking Trail</a></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Nova Scotia has many museums reflecting its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ethnic" title="Ethnic">ethnic</a> heritage, including the <a href="/wiki/Glooscap" title="Glooscap">Glooscap</a> Heritage Centre, <a href="/wiki/Grand-Pr%C3%A9_National_Historic_Site" title="Grand-Pré National Historic Site">Grand-Pré National Historic Site</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hector_(ship)" title="Hector (ship)">Hector Heritage Quay</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Black_Cultural_Centre_for_Nova_Scotia" title="Black Cultural Centre for Nova Scotia">Black Cultural Centre for Nova Scotia</a>. Others museums tell the story of its working history, such as the <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Cape_Breton_Miners%27_Museum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Cape Breton Miners' Museum (page does not exist)">Cape Breton Miners' Museum</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Maritime_Museum_of_the_Atlantic" title="Maritime Museum of the Atlantic">Maritime Museum of the Atlantic</a>.</p>
<p>Nova Scotia is home to several internationally renowned musicians and there are visitor centres in the home towns of <a href="/wiki/Hank_Snow" title="Hank Snow">Hank Snow</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rita_MacNeil" title="Rita MacNeil">Rita MacNeil</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Anne_Murray" title="Anne Murray">Anne Murray Centre</a>. There are also numerous music and cultural festivals such as the <a href="/wiki/Stan_Rogers_Folk_Festival" title="Stan Rogers Folk Festival">Stan Rogers Folk Festival</a>, <a href="/wiki/Celtic_Colours" title="Celtic Colours">Celtic Colours</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_Gaelic_Mod" title="Nova Scotia Gaelic Mod">Nova Scotia Gaelic Mod</a>, <a href="/wiki/Royal_Nova_Scotia_International_Tattoo" title="Royal Nova Scotia International Tattoo">Royal Nova Scotia International Tattoo</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Film_Festival" title="Atlantic Film Festival">Atlantic Film Festival</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Fringe_Festival" title="Atlantic Fringe Festival">Atlantic Fringe Festival</a>.</p>
<p>The province has <a href="/wiki/List_of_National_Historic_Sites_of_Canada_in_Nova_Scotia" title="List of National Historic Sites of Canada in Nova Scotia">87 National Historic Sites of Canada</a>, including the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Habitation_at_Port-Royal" title="Habitation at Port-Royal">Habitation at Port-Royal</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Fortress_of_Louisbourg" title="Fortress of Louisbourg">Fortress of Louisbourg</a> and <a href="/wiki/Citadel_Hill_(Fort_George)" title="Citadel Hill (Fort George)">Citadel Hill (Fort George)</a> in Halifax.</p>
<p>Nova Scotia has two national parks, <a href="/wiki/Kejimkujik_National_Park" title="Kejimkujik National Park">Kejimkujik</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Highlands_National_Park" title="Cape Breton Highlands National Park">Cape Breton Highlands</a>, and many other <a href="/wiki/List_of_protected_areas_of_Nova_Scotia" title="List of protected areas of Nova Scotia">protected areas</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Fundy" title="Bay of Fundy">Bay of Fundy</a> has the highest tidal range in the world, and the iconic <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peggys_Cove,_Nova_Scotia" title="Peggys Cove, Nova Scotia">Peggys Cove</a> is internationally recognized and receives 600,000 plus visitors a year.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup></p>
<p>Acadian Skies and Mi'kmaq Lands is a starlight reserve in southwestern Nova Scotia. It is the first certified <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a>-Starlight Tourist Destination. Starlight tourist destinations are locations that offer conditions for observations of stars which are protected from light pollution.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup></p>
<p>Cruise ships pay regular visits to the province. In 2010, Halifax received 261,000 passengers and Sydney 69,000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2010indicators_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-2010indicators-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>A 2008 Nova Scotia tourism campaign included advertising a fictional mobile phone called <a href="/wiki/Pomegranate_(phone)" title="Pomegranate (phone)">Pomegranate</a> and establishing website, which after reading about "new phone" redirected to tourism info about region.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Nova_Scotia&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>The Minister of Education is responsible for the administration and delivery of education, as defined by the Education Act<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup> and other acts relating to colleges, universities and private schools. The powers of the Minister and the Department of Education are defined by the Ministerial regulations and constrained by the Governor-In-Council regulations.</p>
<p>Nova Scotia has more than 450 public schools for children. The public system offers primary to Grade 12. There are also private schools in the province. Public education is administered by seven regional school boards, responsible primarily for English instruction and French immersion, and also province-wide by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conseil_Scolaire_Acadien_Provincial" title="Conseil Scolaire Acadien Provincial">Conseil Scolaire Acadien Provincial</a>, which administers French instruction to students for whom the primary language is French.</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_Community_College" title="Nova Scotia Community College">Nova Scotia Community College</a> system has 13 campuses around the province. The community college, with its focus on training and education, was established in 1988 by amalgamating the province's former vocational schools.</p>
<p>In addition to its community college system the province has 10 universities, including <a href="/wiki/Dalhousie_University" title="Dalhousie University">Dalhousie University</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_King%27s_College" title="University of King's College">University of King's College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Saint_Mary%27s_University_(Halifax)" title="Saint Mary's University (Halifax)">Saint Mary's University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mount_Saint_Vincent_University" title="Mount Saint Vincent University">Mount Saint Vincent University</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia_College_of_Art_and_Design" title="Nova Scotia College of Art and Design">NSCAD University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Acadia_University" title="Acadia University">Acadia University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_Sainte-Anne" title="Université Sainte-Anne">Université Sainte-Anne</a>, <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Saint_Francis_Xavier_University" title="Saint Francis Xavier University">Saint Francis Xavier University</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_University" title="Cape Breton University">Cape Breton University</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_School_of_Theology" title="Atlantic School of Theology">Atlantic School of Theology</a>.</p>
<p>There are also more than 90 registered private commercial colleges in Nova Scotia.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup></p>

Dover Publications. <a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-486-21703-5" title="Special:BookSources/0-486-21703-5">0-486-21703-5</a></cite><span class="Z3988" title="ctx_ver=Z39.88-2004&amp;rfr_id=info%3Asid%2Fen.wikipedia.org%3ANova+Scotia&amp;rft.aufirst=Helen&amp;rft.aulast=Creighton&amp;rft.btitle=Songs+and+Ballads+from+Nova+Scotia&amp;rft.date=1966&amp;rft.genre=book&amp;rft.isbn=0-486-21703-5&amp;rft.pub=Dover+Publications&amp;rft_id=https%3A%2F%2Fbooks.google.com%2Fbooks%3Fid%3DZJAAC_9ykKQC%26lpg%3DPP1%26dq%3DNova%2520Scotia%26pg%3DPP1%23v%3Donepage%26q%26f%3Dtrue&amp;rft_val_fmt=info%3Aofi%2Ffmt%3Akev%3Amtx%3Abook"><span style="display:none;"> </span></span></li>
<li>Griffiths, Naomi. E. S. <i><a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=cG4wSmIlziYC&amp;lpg=PP1&amp;dq=From%20Migrant%20to%20Acadian%2C%201604-1755%3A%20A%20North%20American%20Border%20People'&amp;pg=PP1#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=true" rel="nofollow">From Migrant to Acadian, 1604–1755: A North American Border People</a></i>. Montreal and Kingston, McGill / Queen's University Press, 2004.</li>
<li>Grenier, John. <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=jVG5h6G5fWMC&amp;lpg=PP1&amp;dq=The%20Far%20Reaches%20of%20Empire.%20%20War%20in%20Nova%20Scotia%2C%201710-1760&amp;pg=PP1#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=true" rel="nofollow">The Far Reaches of Empire. War in Nova Scotia, 1710–1760</a>. University of Oklahoma Press, Norman, 2008. (<a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9780806138763" title="Special:BookSources/9780806138763">9780806138763</a>)</li>
<li>Landry, Peter. The Lion &amp; The Lily. Vol. 1, Trafford Publishing, Victoria, BC., 2007. (<a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/1425154506" title="Special:BookSources/1425154506">1425154506</a>)</li>
<li>Murdoch, Beamish. <a class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=k68NAAAAQAAJ&amp;dq=A%20History%20of%20Nova%20Scotia%2C&amp;pg=PP1#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=trueA" rel="nofollow">History of Nova Scotia, Or Acadie</a>. Vol 2. BiblioBazaar, LaVergne, TN, 1865.</li>
<li>Pryke, Kenneth G. <i>Nova Scotia and Confederation, 1864–74</i> (1979) (<a href="/wiki/International_Standard_Book_Number" title="International Standard Book Number">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/0-8020-5389-0" title="Special:BookSources/0-8020-5389-0">0-8020-5389-0</a>)</li>
